## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which most commonly arise in constitutive laws for solids describing elastic/plastic stress–strain response with temperature-dependent stiffness, yield stress, and thermal softening/expansion effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelastic Hooke’s law (1D): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (elastic stress with thermal expansion strain subtraction)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear elastic): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (stiffness varies approximately linearly with temperature over a range)
- Thermal softening modulus (exponential): sigma = (c0 * exp(c1 * T)) * epsilon (temperature-activated softening/stiffening via exponential E(T))
- Nonlinear elasticity (quadratic): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (small-to-moderate strain nonlinearity with T-dependence)
- Ramberg–Osgood-type (implicit form; explicit surrogate): sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (smooth transition from linear to nonlinear with thermal factor)
- Hollomon/Ludwik hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (strain hardening multiplied by temperature softening factor)
- Voce-type saturation hardening with thermal factor: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon))) * exp(c3 * T) (hardening saturates at large strain; temperature scales flow stress)
- Power-law hardening with temperature-shifted strain: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1 * T)**c2 (effective strain offset by temperature-dependent term)
- Thermoelastic with quadratic thermal strain: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - (c1 * (T - c2) + c3 * (T - c2)**2)) (nonlinear thermal expansion effect)
- Piecewise elastic–plastic (structure): sigma = min((c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon, (c2 * exp(c3 * T)) + c4 * epsilon**c5) (elastic up to yield, then hardening/softening)
- Hyperelastic-style polynomial in strain invariants (1D proxy): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon + c2 * epsilon**3) (odd-power nonlinearity typical of elastic energy expansions)
- Log-type strain hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * log(c2 * epsilon + 1)) * exp(c3 * T) (log hardening at larger strains; thermal scaling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent stiffness → multiply epsilon by a T-dependent modulus term such as (c0 + c1*T) or c0*exp(c1*T).
- Thermal expansion/thermal strain offset → sigma depends on (epsilon - alpha(T)*(T - T0)), often appearing as epsilon minus a T-shift term.
- Thermal softening of flow stress → sigma decreases with increasing T via exp(c*T) with c < 0 or via a decreasing rational factor like 1/(1 + c*T).
- Elastic–plastic transition → use piecewise/min/max structures combining an elastic branch (E(T)*epsilon) and a plastic/hardening branch.
- Strain hardening → increasing sigma with epsilon via epsilon**n, log(1 + c*epsilon), or (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) saturation forms.
- Saturation at large strain (dynamic recovery/Voce-like) → sigma approaches an asymptote using (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or similar sigmoids in epsilon.
- Coupled thermo-mechanical nonlinearity → include interaction terms like T*epsilon, T*epsilon**2, or (epsilon + c*T)**n to represent temperature shifting the apparent strain scale.
- Different regimes across temperature (e.g., below/above transition) → piecewise parameters or switched functional forms with thresholds in T (not just smooth polynomials).
